<div id="review_467773262" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/467773262" />
    <a title="Cj Wilkins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12030166-cj-wilkins"><img alt="Cj Wilkins" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/467773262?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cj Wilkins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cj Wilkins" href="/user/show/12030166-cj-wilkins">Cj Wilkins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062082077" href="/book/show/11875502-grimalkin-the-witch-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer467773262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2343095259394140665">Grimalkin the Witch Assasin is the 9th book in The Last Apprentice series. The series follows the story of the people of the light battling the denizens of the dark. This version of the series follows the witch assassin, Grimalkin, of the Malkin witch clan. Although Grimalkin is a dark witch, her lifetime goal is to destroy the devil himself: The Fiend. In the previous Last Apprentice book, Grimalkin and a Spook's apprentice named Tom Ward, bound the Fiend in a pit with silver alloy stakes. Grim</span>
  <span id="freeText2343095259394140665" style="display:none">Grimalkin the Witch Assasin is the 9th book in The Last Apprentice series. The series follows the story of the people of the light battling the denizens of the dark. This version of the series follows the witch assassin, Grimalkin, of the Malkin witch clan. Although Grimalkin is a dark witch, her lifetime goal is to destroy the devil himself: The Fiend. In the previous Last Apprentice book, Grimalkin and a Spook's apprentice named Tom Ward, bound the Fiend in a pit with silver alloy stakes. Grimalkin separated his head from his body and if the head of the Fiend is reunited with the body he will walk the Earth freely once more. In this book Grimalkin is keeping the head of the Fiend safe from his servants who have made a special creature called a kretch whose one goal is to kill Grimalkin and take the Fiends head back to his body. Grimalkin fights the kretch a few times throughout the book and with the help of her apprentice Thorne and a fellow witch named Alice she kills the kretch. Killing the kretch wasn't easy though and the final battle cost Thorne's life. Now that the head of the Fiend is back in Grimalkin's possession, she must keep it safe until Tom Ward can find a way to destroy the Fiend once and for all.<br /><br />Grimalkin the Witch Assassin is a great book and I really enjoyed it. I would recommend it to anyone who likes fighting and action and adventure. I would recommend reading the other Last Apprentice books first though, because if you don't you will be extremely confused. I also recommend this book to anyone who liked the Harry Potter series, as it has the same characteristics to it. I can't wait to read the next book in the series to see if Tom Ward and Grimalkin can finally destroy the Fiend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2343095259394140665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2518749150" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2518749150" />
    <a title="Chelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32513439-chelle"><img alt="Chelle" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2518749150?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelle" href="/user/show/32513439-chelle">Chelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2518749150&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2518749150" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17450420674723191276">Ok - so this is a cross between a review and a summary of the book. This picks up right where book #8 left off although it is from the point of view of Grimalkin. There are many plot twists and turns - a few of which I did not see coming. I personally enjoyed this book and rate it 5/5. It provided some backstory to Grimalkin as well as introducing an additional character who I consider to be a "mini-Grimalkin".<br/><br/>So - Grimalkin has the fiends head and is on the run pursued by servants of the fiend </span>
  <span id="freeText17450420674723191276" style="display:none">Ok - so this is a cross between a review and a summary of the book. This picks up right where book #8 left off although it is from the point of view of Grimalkin. There are many plot twists and turns - a few of which I did not see coming. I personally enjoyed this book and rate it 5/5. It provided some backstory to Grimalkin as well as introducing an additional character who I consider to be a "mini-Grimalkin".<br /><br />So - Grimalkin has the fiends head and is on the run pursued by servants of the fiend who want to kill her and reunite the fiends head with his body in Ireland. She has been able to fight off anything she needs to up until this point when she senses something 'unknown' tailing her causing her to reach out to Agnes Sowerbutts asking her to Scry and see what is following her. Agnes agrees and when she reaches back out to Grimalkin she tells her that the unknown creature behind her is a Kretch whose Father is a demon - Tanaki - who is constantly evolving created to kill her and obtain the fiends head. She also reveals that should Grimalkin turn and fight the creature it will end in her death at this point in time. Unfortunately Grimalkin is forced to turn and fight and hamstrings the creature (though it recovers later on) and though she tries to make it a quick fight to disable her pursuer instead of killing it. <br /><br />The kretch scratches Grimalkin which weakens her - she learns that the kretch's claws are imbued with poison and tries to make it back to Pendle where she can ask Agnes (who is also more than adept at healing, just like she is with scrying) to heal her, however she is weakened and unable to make it so she summons one of the few people she knows she can trust - Thorne, her 'apprentice' she has been training in secret to become the next Malkin clan assassin. Thorne manages to get her to Agnes who i able to heal her, while she was still under the influence of the poison Grimalkin astrally projected to Malkin Tower to check and see what the Lamia witches who were in control of the tower were doing. Agnes reveals that Grimalkin may never be 100% what she was before which proves to be correct as she is subject to random bouts of weakness. Once she recovers enough Grimalkin and Thorne set off for Malkin Tower to consult with the Lamias who offer them refuge from their pursuers. <br /><br />Once they arrive Agnes reaches out to warn them that their pursuers are still after them and are at her door likely intent on killing her. Their pursuers soon arrive with Agnes in tow, threatening to kill her unless Grimalkin hands over the fiends head - she refuses. Wynde (one of the Lamias) flies down to attach them but is killed. In retaliation Grimalkin puts out one of the fiends eyes threatening to put the other one out if they do not flee. The fiend manages to send a message out to all gathered threatening them that due to what happened he will seek retaliation thus convincing them to comply and flee. Grimalkin and Thorne inform the other Lamia (Slake) what has occurred and inform her that they will be leaving, setting out for Clitheroe; an area that has become dangerous after the war that ravaged the county and is known for cut throats and robbers. <br /><br />Once there Thorne and Grimalkin are pretty near instantly attacked and manage to drive off their enemies saving the son (Will) of a local knight in the process. Will promises them shelter and help at his home if they return him to his father - they do so and the father reluctantly does so as he is honor bound to do so as a result of his son giving his word. They inform the knight who they are and what they are doing and discover he is famous and slayed a worme with the aid of special armor. He agrees to help them and offers them not just refuge for the siege that will likely follow but the help of his men who are masters at their trades. He faces opposition by his priest in the town who distrusts the witches. <br /><br />Their pursuers follow them and the kretch calls a challenge of single combat to the knight who is honor bound to accept though Grimalkin and Thorne try to talk him out of it but are unsuccessful. He goes to face the kretch and is mortally wounded; Grimalkin, Thorne and his men bring him back into his home but determine the wound is to his head and the best thing that can be done for him at this point is to make him comfortable until he dies. One he dies Will becomes vengeful, angry at the death of his father. <br /><br />Grimalkin and Thorne prepare to leave as they know that the priest will become guardian of will and owner of the grounds, however they are too slow and are captured after being overwhelmed by attackers. Once Grimalkin awakens in the dungeons she manages to escape and make her way out to where Thorne is being tortured killing anyone who stands in her way. They flee - leaving Will alive as they leave warning him that he is now in charge of everything his father was and he needs to rule fairly. <br /><br />As Thorne and Grimalkin continue - heading for the with dell, Thorne asks Grimalkin to tell her the story of how she became the Malkin Clan witch assassin. Grimalkin obliges - she trained and then challenged the then assassin who used the witch dell (and conspired with dead witches) as her 'killing ground' with various traps hidden - Grimalkin had swept the area in the weeks leading up to her showdown and goes in confident that she will win facing down dead witches as she makes her way further into the witch dell, however she falls into a pit that was dug right before the challenge filled with spikes. She manages to contort her body to minimize the damage and as her challenger comes down to strangle her and finish her off Grimalkin wiggles the spike back and forth until she breaks it off and uses it to kill the current witch assassin. <br /><br />Once they arrive in the witch dell, planning to use the dead witches to thin their attackers out, they seek out Agnes to see how she is, however they are unable to go with their original plan and their pursuers burn the witch dell to flush them out where they are forced to stand and fight. Grimalkin is subject to a bout of weakness and unable to fight so Thorne steps up and tries to kill the Kretch but is overpowered and then killed - her thumb bones are taken while she is still alive. They take the fiends head and leave. <br /><br />When Grimalkin comes back to she discovers Thorne is dead and resolves to kill every one of the people involved in the attack. She goes to Chippenden to ask Alice to help her - Alice heals her (completely) and 'lends' her magic. They set off and kill the kretch and all of the others (some slowly and painfully in retaliation for Thorne) and recover the head of the fiend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17450420674723191276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14808911349553509167">As mentioned in a previous posting in regards to this 'series', I was given almost the entire THE LAST APPRENTICE series.<br/><br/>And again, I have to state that this is NOT FOR YOUNG READERS and should be for strictly GRADE 8 and up.<br/><br/>It contains Black Magic, Demons, Witches, and all sorts of bloodletting, dismemberment, and much violence depicted within it's pages. Still can't believe it's zeroed in on basicly a Young Age Group. For mature Teens and such? Yes, by all means as this is proving to be a very</span>
  <span id="freeText14808911349553509167" style="display:none">As mentioned in a previous posting in regards to this 'series', I was given almost the entire THE LAST APPRENTICE series.<br /><br />And again, I have to state that this is NOT FOR YOUNG READERS and should be for strictly GRADE 8 and up.<br /><br />It contains Black Magic, Demons, Witches, and all sorts of bloodletting, dismemberment, and much violence depicted within it's pages. Still can't believe it's zeroed in on basicly a Young Age Group. For mature Teens and such? Yes, by all means as this is proving to be a very entertaining read. Especially this particular volume concerning one of the Series best crafted characters and my favorite: Grimalkin. Having a book/novel entirely based on her and where her standings is within this series is quite a formable high-light for fans of THE LAST APPRENTICE. Her own story (like all the other LAST APPRENTICE books) is a fast read and enjoyable. Not a stand-alone book because the story continues where the last novel left off, but with what she had to do in a continuation of the over-all Story/Plot. I strongly suggest reading all the prior books before this.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5587477632998123627">It is a sad day when I read one of my beloved "Spook's" books and don't like it!! I got to chapter 6 (which is 60 pages in) and decided to give up and read the last 2 chapters to see what happens in the end. I must admit though that this story is written from a different characters point of view and I think that's why I don't like it. I don't really like Grimalkin, the witch assassin, I prefer to hear the tale from Tom Ward, the spook's young apprentice. I also enjoy The Spook's (John Gregory) h</span>
  <span id="freeText5587477632998123627" style="display:none">It is a sad day when I read one of my beloved "Spook's" books and don't like it!! I got to chapter 6 (which is 60 pages in) and decided to give up and read the last 2 chapters to see what happens in the end. I must admit though that this story is written from a different characters point of view and I think that's why I don't like it. I don't really like Grimalkin, the witch assassin, I prefer to hear the tale from Tom Ward, the spook's young apprentice. I also enjoy The Spook's (John Gregory) humor and wit, which is missing from this installment as all three main characters aren't really featured much. This is the ninth book in the series and hopefully it doesn't matter that I skipped it when I go to read the next one when it comes out later this year. I feel devastated that I'm giving this 1 star :-( </span>

<div id="review_1805131189" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1805131189" />
    <a title="Chandler Corpus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35527641-chandler-corpus"><img alt="Chandler Corpus" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1805131189?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chandler Corpus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chandler Corpus" href="/user/show/35527641-chandler-corpus">Chandler Corpus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062082077" href="/book/show/11875502-grimalkin-the-witch-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1805131189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2101496864345152041">In this book, Thomas continues his Apprenticeship as a Spook, someone who fights the dark and boy is it a hard one. It continues the story of The Last Apprentice but this time, in Grimalkin's, a witch assassin who has temporarily allied with Thomas to destroy the Fiend, point of view. It's always nice to know a little backstory from a character who actually kills for a living. What made me really like the book is that I noticed that the writing was different than in Thomas's point of view. There</span>
  <span id="freeText2101496864345152041" style="display:none">In this book, Thomas continues his Apprenticeship as a Spook, someone who fights the dark and boy is it a hard one. It continues the story of The Last Apprentice but this time, in Grimalkin's, a witch assassin who has temporarily allied with Thomas to destroy the Fiend, point of view. It's always nice to know a little backstory from a character who actually kills for a living. What made me really like the book is that I noticed that the writing was different than in Thomas's point of view. There wasn't any words that I was used to popping up. And the way the story was told was different also and that shocked me. It seems as if each character has a different way of writing in their own point of view. This was by far one of the best books Iv'e read in this series and I hope there will be more books like this in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2101496864345152041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1166897824328541318">I think this is my favorite book from Spook's Apprentice Series, ironically this is not even about Spook's Apprentice<br/><br/>But really I love Grimalkin and to read the book from her point of view is entertaining. She's totally bad ass, courageous, strong, but still have a soft side in her. <br/><br/>And I can't not love Thorne, she's witch assassin apprentice, Grimalkin's protege. Trust me, you gotta love her character<br/><br/>Beside Grimalkin's adventure in this book I love how Delaney give us a lil bit snippet about Gr</span>
  <span id="freeText1166897824328541318" style="display:none">I think this is my favorite book from Spook's Apprentice Series, ironically this is not even about Spook's Apprentice<br /><br />But really I love Grimalkin and to read the book from her point of view is entertaining. She's totally bad ass, courageous, strong, but still have a soft side in her. <br /><br />And I can't not love Thorne, she's witch assassin apprentice, Grimalkin's protege. Trust me, you gotta love her character<br /><br />Beside Grimalkin's adventure in this book I love how Delaney give us a lil bit snippet about Grimalkin's past like how she become witch assassin, her past with the fiend, and many more. <br /><br />"My speed in combat is not dark magic; it is the magic of my being, the magic of who I am. I am Grimalkin! </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1054263822&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1054263822" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6429685696167544334">Excellent book. It deviates from the main storyline of Tom Ward while still being counted as one of the series; this runs parallel to it, adding and never taking away.<br/> I was very worried I would have to say goodbye to my favourite character with this reading, but instead I was surprised by the death of a new, and welcome, addition. (I had actually held myself back from liking Thorne too much because I was SURE she was going to turn against Grimalkin. So much for intuition.) I cannot wait for wha</span>
  <span id="freeText6429685696167544334" style="display:none">Excellent book. It deviates from the main storyline of Tom Ward while still being counted as one of the series; this runs parallel to it, adding and never taking away.<br /> I was very worried I would have to say goodbye to my favourite character with this reading, but instead I was surprised by the death of a new, and welcome, addition. (I had actually held myself back from liking Thorne too much because I was SURE she was going to turn against Grimalkin. So much for intuition.) I cannot wait for what comes next in this fantastic series. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Z5uIQCXiXSH1V3d09DbZBqpLvoqj/m38GSjTyyB1BULCTVibIh2J8rsJtQ7S4P8WbyLO4OypvrByzxYtcpptQw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kC9PvgztekMYb3PlaW2IkNNOSXFjTN2d3rhqH/079q01+Z9lCxKukFYxsZ9Pu66AFic5GywbDtG1X6/5r9SerA==')})
  }
//]]>

Mii de spanioli republicani au plecat în exil după ce forțele naționaliste conduse de Franco au învins în Războiul Civil (1936–1939). Dintre cei fugiți peste hotare, 7 500 de spanioli au fost capturați de germani în Franța, după ocuparea țării în timpul celui de-al Doilea Război Mondial. Au fost luați prizonieri și apoi deportați în lagăr, unde Boix, lucrător în laboratorul fotografic de la Mauthausen, împreună cu alți deținuți au reușit să salveze de la distrugere circa 2 000 de negative cu atrocități comise de ofițerii SS. Multe dintre fotografiile colecției au fost utilizate ca probe în cadrul proceselor postbelice intentate foștilor demnitari naziști. La câțiva ani după încheierea războiului, fotograful – a cărui sănătate s-a șubrezit foarte mult din cauza condițiilor inumane din detenție – a murit. Datorită eforturilor tânărului hotărât și curajos, s-au păstrat însă o parte dintre dovezile ce au acuzat și au demascat un sistem concentraționar teribil și o ideologie criminală.\n\n„Fotograful de la Mauthausen, regizat de Mar Targarona, fără a fi un blockbuster, a reușit să mă tulbure și să mă sensibilizeze. La finalul filmului sunt prezentate adevăratele fotografii ale poveștii. Una mi-a atras în mod deosebit atenția, cea care înfățișează cadavrul șefului lagărului, linșat și aruncat în gardul de sârmă ghimpată. Fără milă, așa cum ar trebui să fie, în numele justiției și al răzbunării.” Carlos Boyero, El País\n\n„În momentul înfrângerii germanilor, dintr-un hoț de fotografii oficiale, Boix a devenit fotoreporter al eliberării deținuților. Volumul Fotograful de la Mauthausen, ilustrat cu fotografiile salvate de la distrugere și cu cele realizate de Boix însuși, demonstrează cum este posibil sa îmbini în mod armonios mărturiile cu       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/146374.Joseph_Delaney">About Joseph Delaney</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/146374.Joseph_Delaney"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1376358484p3/146374.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/146374.Joseph_Delaney">Joseph Delaney
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
3,426
followers
</div>

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10995034390766506468">Joseph Delaney is a full time writer living in Lancashire, in the heart of Boggart territory.<br/>He is the author of Wardstone Chronicles, Starblade Chronicles, Arena 13, Aberrations and a new book came out in April 2020, Brother Wulf. This is a new spooks story featuring Tom and Alice, but introducing a new character, a young monk called Brother Wulf. <br/><br/>He first got the idea for the Spooks series when </span>
  <span id="freeText10995034390766506468" style="display:none">Joseph Delaney is a full time writer living in Lancashire, in the heart of Boggart territory.<br />He is the author of Wardstone Chronicles, Starblade Chronicles, Arena 13, Aberrations and a new book came out in April 2020, Brother Wulf. This is a new spooks story featuring Tom and Alice, but introducing a new character, a young monk called Brother Wulf. <br /><br />He first got the idea for the Spooks series when he moved to the village where he lives now and discovered there was a local boggart - ‘a man like me needs boggarts around’. He made a note in his notebook ‘a story about a man who hunts boggarts’ and years later when he had to come up with an idea at short notice developed this into ‘The Spook’s Apprentice’, the first book in the series.<br />He continues to draw upon the folklore of Lancashire and has acquired much local knowledge over the years which he tweaks and modifies to create his fictional world. Another source of inspiration has been Lancashire's varied and atmospheric landscape. Many of the locations in the County are based on actual places in Lancashire. <br />In the early days of his writing career Joseph worked as a teacher at a Sixth Form College: his subjects were English, Film and Media Studies. He used to get up early and write every morning before work. That way he could write a book a year – which promptly got rejected! When the Americans bought the series he decided to give up teaching and write full time. <br />Prior to teaching he worked as an engineer in his twenties, completing an apprenticeship just like Tom Ward in the spook’s books.<br />Joseph describes his method of writing as a process of discovery. He doesn’t plot too far ahead and often doesn’t know what is going to happen until he writes it down. In other words he makes it up as he goes along. He prefers writing dialogue to description, in which he says he is a minimalist and leaves much to the reader’s imagination. <br />Joseph has three children and nine grandchildren and is a wonderful public speaker available for conference, library and bookshop events.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2330711.The_Spook_s_Apprentice" title="The Spook's Apprentice" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Apprentice</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17426629.The_Spook_s_Curse" title="The Spook's Curse" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Curse</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17426189.The_Spook_s_Secret" title="The Spook's Secret" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Secret</a> have all been shortlisted for the Lancashire children's Book for the Year Award. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2330711.The_Spook_s_Apprentice" title="The Spook's Apprentice" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Apprentice</a> is the winner of both the Sefton Book Award and the Hampshire Book Award.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.josephdelaneyauthor.com">www.josephdelaneyauthor.com</a><br /><br /><br /><i>from <a href="http://www.rbooks.co.uk/author.aspx?id=15205" rel="nofollow noopener">publisher's website</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10995034390766506468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
